<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">Return of capital to shareholders was $1.5&nbsp;billion </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">CHICAGO, Ill. &#150; April&nbsp;27, 2021 &#150; Mondel&#275;z International, Inc. (Nasdaq: MDLZ) today reported its first quarter 2021
results. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">&#147;Our first quarter results demonstrate that we are emerging from the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">COVID-19</FONT>
pandemic stronger, as we continue to build upon our track record of robust growth, profitability and cash generation,&#148; said Dirk Van de Put, Chairman and Chief Executive Officer. &#147;We saw continued improvement across emerging markets,
healthy demand in developed markets and another quarter of strong share performance. We remain squarely focused on accelerating growth by further strengthening our core brand and expanding our presence in high-growth channels, categories and
adjacencies. Our strategy is working, and our business is better positioned than ever before.&#148; </P>
</DIV></Center>

<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I><U>First Quarter Commentary </U></I></P>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Net revenues</B> increased 7.9&nbsp;percent driven by Organic Net Revenue growth of 3.8&nbsp;percent,
favorable currency, and incremental sales from the company&#146;s acquisitions of Give&nbsp;&amp; Go and Hu. Volume and pricing drove Organic Net Revenue growth, partially offset by unfavorable mix. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Gross profit </B>increased $515&nbsp;million, while gross profit margin increased 450 basis points to
41.0&nbsp;percent, primarily driven by favorable year-over-year change in <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> gains/losses from currency and commodity derivatives. Adjusted Gross Profit<SUP
STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">1</SUP> increased $134&nbsp;million at constant currency, while Adjusted Gross Profit margin remained flat at 39.6&nbsp;percent due to higher raw material costs and unfavorable product mix, offset by higher
pricing and manufacturing productivity. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Operating income </B>increased $427&nbsp;million and operating income margin was 17.7&nbsp;percent, up 490
basis points primarily due to favorable year-over-year change in <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> gains/losses from currency and commodity derivatives and higher Adjusted Operating Income<SUP
STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">1</SUP>, partially offset by higher restructuring expenses. Adjusted Operating Income increased $142&nbsp;million at constant currency, and Adjusted Operating Income margin increased 140 basis points to
17.9&nbsp;percent primarily driven by lower overhead costs, partially offset by increased advertising and consumer promotions spend. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Diluted EPS</B> was $0.68, up 33.3&nbsp;percent, primarily due to <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> gains from derivatives versus losses in the prior year, lapping the prior-year loss on interest rate swaps and an increase in Adjusted EPS, partially offset by a loss on debt extinguishment,
higher Simplify to Grow program costs and lapping the prior-year gain on equity method investment transactions. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">

share repurchases, partially offset by lower equity method investment earnings and higher taxes primarily due to changes in the company&#146;s mix of earnings. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>

listen-only webcast will be provided at <U>www.mondelezinternational.com</U>. An archive of the webcast will be available on the company&#146;s web site. The company will be live tweeting the event at <U>www.twitter.com/MDLZ</U>. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>About Mondel&#275;z International </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Mondel&#275;z International, Inc. (Nasdaq: MDLZ) empowers people to snack right in over 150 countries around the world. With 2020 net revenues
of approximately $27&nbsp;billion, MDLZ is leading the future of snacking with iconic global and local brands such as <I>Oreo</I>, <I>belVita</I> and <I>LU</I> biscuits; <I>Cadbury Dairy Milk</I>, <I>Milka</I> and <I>Toblerone</I> chocolate; <I>Sour
Patch Kids</I> candy and <I>Trident</I> gum. Mondel&#275;z International is a proud member of the Standard and Poor&#146;s 500, Nasdaq 100 and Dow Jones Sustainability Index. Visit <U>www.mondelezinternational.com</U> or follow the company on
Twitter at <U>www.twitter.com/MDLZ</U>. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>End Notes </B></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Additional Definitions </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Emerging markets consist of the Latin America region in its entirety; the Asia, Middle East and Africa region excluding Australia, New Zealand
and Japan; and the following countries from the Europe region: Russia, Ukraine, Turkey, Kazakhstan, Georgia, Poland, Czech Republic, Slovak Republic, Hungary, Bulgaria, Romania, the Baltics and the East Adriatic countries. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Developed markets include the entire North America region, the Europe region excluding the countries included in the emerging markets
definition, and Australia, New Zealand and Japan from the Asia, Middle East and Africa region. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Forward-Looking Statements </B></P>

&#147;expect,&#148; &#147;may,&#148; &#147;would,&#148; &#147;could,&#148; &#147;estimate,&#148; &#147;outlook&#148; and similar expressions are intended to identify the company&#146;s forward-looking statements, including, but not limited to,
statements about: the impact of and volatility resulting from the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">COVID-19</FONT> pandemic; the company&#146;s strategy and the prospects for the business; the company&#146;s future performance, including its future
revenue growth, earnings per share and cash flow; currency and the effect of currency translation on the company&#146;s results of operations;&nbsp;the company&#146;s long-term algorithm; and the company&#146;s outlook, including 2021 Organic Net
Revenue growth, Adjusted EPS growth and Free Cash Flow. These forward-looking statements are subject to a number of risks and uncertainties, many of which are beyond the company&#146;s control, and many of these risks and uncertainties are currently
amplified by and may continue to be amplified by the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">COVID-19</FONT> pandemic. Important factors that could cause the company&#146;s actual results to differ materially from those indicated in the company&#146;s

<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always">
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">


<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>Mondel&#275;z International, Inc. and Subsidiaries </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>Reconciliation of GAAP and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-GAAP</FONT> Financial Measures </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>(Unaudited) </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company reports its
financial results in accordance with accounting principles generally accepted in the United States (&#147;GAAP&#148;). However, management believes that also presenting certain <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures
provides additional information to facilitate the comparison of the company&#146;s historical operating results and trends in its underlying operating results, and provides additional transparency on how the company evaluates its business.
Management uses these <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures in making financial, operating and planning decisions and in evaluating the company&#146;s performance. The company also believes that presenting these
measures allows investors to view its performance using the same measures that the company uses in evaluating its financial and business performance and trends. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company considers quantitative and qualitative factors in assessing whether to adjust for the impact of items that may be significant or that could affect
an understanding of its ongoing financial and business performance and trends. The adjustments generally fall within the following categories: acquisition&nbsp;&amp; divestiture activities, gains and losses on intangible asset sales and <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-cash</FONT> impairments, major program restructuring activities, constant currency and related adjustments, major program financing and hedging activities and other major items affecting comparability of operating
results. See below for a description of adjustments to the company&#146;s U.S. GAAP financial measures included herein. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-GAAP</FONT> information should be considered as supplemental in nature and is not meant to be considered in isolation or
as a substitute for the related financial information prepared in accordance with U.S. GAAP. In addition, the company&#146;s <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures may not be the same as or comparable to similar <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> measures presented by other companies. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>DEFINITIONS OF THE COMPANY&#146;S
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">NON-GAAP</FONT> FINANCIAL MEASURES </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company&#146;s <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial
measures and corresponding metrics reflect how the company evaluates its operating results currently and provide improved comparability of operating results. As new events or circumstances arise, these definitions could change. When these
definitions change, the company provides the updated definitions and presents the related <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> historical results on a comparable basis. When items no longer impact the company&#146;s current or future
presentation of <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> operating results, the company removes these items from its <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> definitions. </P>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>&#147;Organic Net Revenue&#148;</B> is defined as net revenues excluding the impacts of acquisitions,
divestitures and currency rate fluctuations. The company also evaluates Organic Net Revenue growth from emerging markets and developed markets. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>&#147;Adjusted Gross Profit&#148;</B> is defined as gross profit excluding the impacts of the Simplify to Grow
Program; acquisition integration costs; the operating results of divestitures; and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> impacts from commodity and forecasted currency transaction derivative
contracts. The company also presents &#147;Adjusted Gross Profit margin,&#148; which is subject to the same adjustments as Adjusted Gross Profit. The company also evaluates growth in the company&#146;s Adjusted Gross Profit on a constant currency
basis. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>&#147;Adjusted Operating Income&#148;</B> and <B>&#147;Adjusted Segment Operating Income&#148;</B> are defined
as operating income (or segment operating income) excluding the impacts of the items listed in the Adjusted Gross Profit definition as well as gains or losses (including <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-cash</FONT> impairment charges) on
goodwill and intangible assets; divestiture or acquisition gains or losses and related divestiture, acquisition and integration costs; costs associated with the JDE Peet&#146;s transaction; remeasurement of net monetary position; impacts from
resolution of tax matters; CEO transition remuneration; Swiss tax reform impacts; and impact from pension participation changes. The company also presents &#147;Adjusted Operating Income margin&#148; and &#147;Adjusted Segment Operating Income
margin,&#148; which are subject to the same adjustments as Adjusted Operating Income and Adjusted Segment Operating Income. The company also evaluates growth in the company&#146;s Adjusted Operating Income and Adjusted Segment Operating Income on a
constant currency basis. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>&#147;Adjusted EPS&#148;</B> is defined as diluted EPS attributable to Mondel&#275;z International from
continuing operations excluding the impacts of the items listed in the Adjusted Operating Income definition, as well as losses on debt extinguishment and related expenses; gains or losses on equity method investment transactions; net earnings from
divestitures; gains or losses on interest rate swaps no longer designated as accounting cash flow hedges due to changed financing and hedging plans; and U.S. and Swiss tax reform impacts. Similarly, within Adjusted EPS, the company&#146;s equity
method investment net earnings exclude its proportionate share of its investees&#146; significant operating and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-operating</FONT> items. The tax impact of each of the items excluded from the company&#146;s GAAP
results was computed based on the facts and tax assumptions associated with each item, and such impacts have also been excluded from Adjusted EPS. The company also evaluates growth in the company&#146;s Adjusted EPS on a constant currency basis.
</P></TD></TR></TABLE>

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>&#147;Free Cash Flow&#148;</B> is defined as net cash provided by operating activities less capital
expenditures. Free Cash Flow is the company&#146;s primary measure used to monitor its cash flow performance. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">See the attached
schedules for supplemental financial data and corresponding reconciliations of the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures referred to above to the most comparable GAAP financial measures for the three months and year
ended December&nbsp;31, 2020 and December&nbsp;31, 2019. See Items Impacting Comparability of Operating Results below for more information about the items referenced in these definitions that specifically impacted the company&#146;s results. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>SEGMENT OPERATING INCOME </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company uses segment
operating income to evaluate segment performance and allocate resources. The company believes it is appropriate to disclose this measure to help investors analyze segment performance and trends. Segment operating income excludes unrealized gains and
losses on hedging activities (which are a component of cost of sales), general corporate expenses (which are a component of selling, general and administrative expenses), amortization of intangibles, gains and losses on divestitures and
acquisition-related costs (which are a component of selling, general and administrative expenses) in all periods presented. The company excludes these items from segment operating income in order to provide better transparency of its segment
operating results. Furthermore, the company centrally manages benefit plan <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-service</FONT> income and interest and other expense, net. Accordingly, the company does not present these items by segment because they
are excluded from the segment profitability measure that management reviews. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>ITEMS IMPACTING COMPARABILITY OF OPERATING RESULTS </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The following information is provided to give qualitative and quantitative information related to items impacting comparability of operating results. The
company identifies these based on how management views the company&#146;s business; makes financial, operating and planning decisions; and evaluates the company&#146;s ongoing performance. In addition, the company discloses the impact of changes in
currency exchange rates on the company&#146;s financial results in order to reflect results on a constant currency basis. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Divestitures,
Divestiture-related costs and Gains/(losses) on divestitures </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Divestitures include completed sales of businesses (including the partial or full
sale of an equity method investment&#151;discussed separately below under the gains and losses on equity method investment transactions section) and exits of major product lines upon completion of a sale or licensing agreement. As the company
records its share of KDP and JDE Peet&#146;s ongoing earnings on a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">one-quarter</FONT> lag basis, any KDP or JDE Peet&#146;s ownership reductions are reflected as divestitures within the company&#146;s <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> results the following quarter. </P> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">The company&#146;s <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> results include the impacts from
last-year&#146;s partial sales of its equity method investments in KDP and JDE Peet&#146;s as if the sales occurred at the beginning of all periods presented. See the section on gains/losses on equity method transactions below for more information.
</P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Acquisitions, Acquisition-related costs and Acquisition integration costs </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On April&nbsp;1, 2021, the company acquired Gourmet Food Holdings Pty Ltd, a leading Australian food company in the premium biscuit and cracker category. The
company incurred acquisition-related costs of $1&nbsp;million during the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2021. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On March&nbsp;25, 2021, the company
acquired a majority interest in Lion/Gemstone Topco Ltd (&#147;Grenade&#148;), a performance nutrition leader in the United Kingdom. The acquisition of Grenade expands the company&#146;s position into the premium nutrition market. The company
incurred acquisition-related costs of $2&nbsp;million during the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2021. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On January&nbsp;4, 2021, the company acquired
the remaining 93% of equity of Hu Master Holdings, a category leader in premium chocolate in the United States, which provides a strategic complement to the company&#146;s snacking portfolio in North America through growth opportunities in chocolate
and other categories in the well-being segment. As a result of acquiring the remaining equity interest, the company consolidated the operation and recorded a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> gain of $9&nbsp;million ($7&nbsp;million <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">after-tax)</FONT> related to stepping up the company&#146;s previously-held $8&nbsp;million (7%) investment to fair value. The acquisition added incremental net revenues of $8&nbsp;million and an operating loss of
$6&nbsp;million in the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2021. The company also incurred acquisition-related costs of $4&nbsp;million during the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2021. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On April&nbsp;1, 2020, the company acquired a majority interest in Give&nbsp;&amp; Go, a North American leader in fully-finished sweet baked goods and owner
of the famous <I><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">two-bite</FONT></I><I><SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">&reg;</SUP></I> brand of brownies and the
<I><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Create-A-Treat</FONT></FONT></I><I><SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">&reg;</SUP></I> brand, known for cookie and gingerbread house decorating kits. The acquisition of
Give&nbsp;&amp; Go provides access to the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">in-store</FONT> bakery channel and expands the </P>
</DIV></Center>


<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always">
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">


<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">
company&#146;s position in broader snacking. The acquisition added incremental net revenues of $106&nbsp;million and operating income of $6&nbsp;million in the three months ended March&nbsp;31,
2021. The company incurred $1&nbsp;million of acquisition-integrations costs in the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2021.The company also incurred acquisition-related costs of $5&nbsp;million in the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2020. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Simplify to Grow Program </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The primary objective of
the Simplify to Grow Program is to reduce the company&#146;s operating cost structure in both its supply chain and overhead costs. The program covers severance as well as asset disposals and other manufacturing and procurement-related <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">one-time</FONT> costs. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Restructuring costs </I></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company recorded restructuring charges of $88&nbsp;million in the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2021 and $15&nbsp;million in the three months ended
March&nbsp;31, 2020 within asset impairment and exit costs and benefit plan <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-service</FONT> income. These charges were for severance and related costs, <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-cash</FONT> asset
write-downs (including accelerated depreciation and asset impairments) and other adjustments, including any gains on sale of restructuring program assets. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Implementation costs </I></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Implementation costs primarily
relate to reorganizing the company&#146;s operations and facilities in connection with its supply chain reinvention program and other identified productivity and cost saving initiatives. The costs include incremental expenses related to the closure
of facilities, costs to terminate certain contracts and the simplification of the company&#146;s information systems. The company recorded implementation costs of $34&nbsp;million in the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2021 and $43&nbsp;million in
the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2020. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> impacts
from commodity and currency derivative contracts </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company excludes unrealized gains and losses <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">(mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> impacts) from outstanding commodity and forecasted currency transaction derivatives from its <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> earnings measures until such time that the related
exposures impact its operating results. The company recorded net unrealized gains on commodity and forecasted currency transaction derivatives of $117&nbsp;million in the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2021 and recorded net unrealized losses of
$184&nbsp;million in the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2020. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Remeasurement of net monetary position </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During the second quarter of 2018, primarily based on published estimates which indicated that Argentina&#146;s three-year cumulative inflation rate exceeded
100%, the company concluded that Argentina became a highly inflationary economy for accounting purposes. As of July&nbsp;1, 2018, the company began to apply highly inflationary accounting for its Argentinian subsidiaries and changed their functional
currency from the Argentinian peso to the U.S. dollar. On July&nbsp;1, 2018, both monetary and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-monetary</FONT> assets and liabilities denominated in Argentinian pesos were remeasured into U.S. dollars. As of each
subsequent balance sheet date, Argentinian peso denominated monetary assets and liabilities were remeasured into U.S. dollars using the exchange rate as of the balance sheet date, with remeasurement and other transaction gains and losses recorded in
net earnings. Within selling, general and administrative expenses, the company recorded remeasurement losses of $5&nbsp;million in the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2021 and $2&nbsp;million in the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2020 related
to the revaluation of the Argentinian peso denominated net monetary position over these periods. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Impact from pension participation changes
</I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The impact from pension participation changes represent the charges incurred when employee groups are withdrawn from multiemployer pension plans
and other changes in employee group pension plan participation. The company excludes these charges from its <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> results because those amounts do not reflect the company&#146;s ongoing pension obligations.
</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On July&nbsp;11, 2019, the company received an undiscounted withdrawal liability assessment related to the company&#146;s complete withdrawal from the
Bakery and Confectionery Union and Industry International Pension Fund totaling $526&nbsp;million and requiring <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pro-rata</FONT> monthly payments over 20 years. The company began making monthly payments during the
third quarter of 2019. The company recorded $3&nbsp;million of accreted interest in the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2021 and $3&nbsp;million in the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2020 on the long-term liability within interest and other
expense, net. As of March&nbsp;31, 2021, the remaining discounted withdrawal liability was $372&nbsp;million, with $14&nbsp;million recorded in other current liabilities and $358&nbsp;million recorded in long-term other liabilities. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Loss on debt extinguishment and related expenses </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On March&nbsp;31, 2021, the company completed an early redemption of Euro (&#128;1,200 million) and U.S. dollar ($992 million) denominated notes. The company
recorded $137&nbsp;million of extinguishment loss and debt-related expenses within interest and other expense, net related to $110&nbsp;million paid in excess of carrying value of the debt and recognizing unamortized discounts and deferred financing
in earnings and $27&nbsp;million foreign currency derivative loss related to the redemption payment at the time of the debt extinguishment. </P>
</DIV></Center>


<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always">
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">


<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Loss related to interest rate swaps </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Within interest and other expense, net, the company recognized a loss related to forward-starting interest rate swaps of $79&nbsp;million ($103&nbsp;million <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax)</FONT> for the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2020 due to the changes in related forecasted debt. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Gains and
losses on equity method investment transactions </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Keurig Dr Pepper Transactions: </I></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On March&nbsp;4, 2020, the company participated in a secondary offering of KDP shares and sold approximately 6.8&nbsp;million shares, which reduced its
ownership interest by 0.5% of total outstanding shares. The company received $185&nbsp;million of proceeds and recorded a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> gain of $71&nbsp;million (or $54&nbsp;million
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">after-tax)</FONT> during the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2020. On August&nbsp;3, 2020, the company sold approximately 14.1&nbsp;million shares of KDP, which reduced its ownership interest by 1.0% of the total
outstanding shares. The company received $414&nbsp;million of proceeds and recorded a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> gain of $181&nbsp;million (or $139&nbsp;million <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">after-tax)</FONT> during the third
quarter of 2020. On September&nbsp;9, 2020, the company sold approximately 12.5&nbsp;million shares of KDP, which reduced its ownership interest by 0.9% of the total outstanding shares. The company received $363&nbsp;million of proceeds and recorded
a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> gain of $154&nbsp;million (or $119&nbsp;million <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">after-tax)</FONT> during the third quarter of 2020. On November&nbsp;17, 2020, the company participated in a secondary
offering of KDP shares and sold approximately 40.0&nbsp;million shares, which reduced the company&#146;s ownership interest by 2.8% of the total outstanding shares. The company received $1,132&nbsp;million of proceeds and recorded a <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> gain of $459&nbsp;million (or $350&nbsp;million <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">after-tax)</FONT> during the fourth quarter of 2020. The company considers these ownership reductions partial divestitures of
its equity method investment in KDP. Therefore, the company has removed the equity method investment net earnings related to this divested portion from its <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial results for Adjusted EPS for all
historical periods presented to facilitate comparison of results. The company&#146;s U.S. GAAP results, which include its equity method investment net earnings from KDP, did not change from what was previously reported. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>JDE Peet&#146;s Transaction: </I></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">In May 2020, JDE
Peet&#146;s B.V. (renamed JDE Peet&#146;s N.V. immediately prior to Settlement (as defined below), &#147;JDE Peet&#146;s&#148;) consummated the offering, listing and trading of its ordinary shares on Euronext Amsterdam, a regulated market operated
by Euronext Amsterdam N.V. (the &#147;admission&#148;). In connection with this transaction, JDE Peet&#146;s and the selling shareholders, including the company, agreed to sell at a price of &#128;31.50 per ordinary share a total of approximately
82.1&nbsp;million ordinary shares, including ordinary shares subject to an over-allotment option. The ordinary shares were listed and first traded on May&nbsp;29, 2020, and payment for, and delivery of, the ordinary shares sold in the offering
(excluding ordinary shares subject to the over-allotment option) took place on June&nbsp;2, 2020 (&#147;Settlement&#148;). </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Prior to Settlement, the
company exchanged its 26.4% ownership interest in JDE for a 26.5% equity interest in JDE Peet&#146;s. The company did not invest new capital in connection with the transaction and the exchange was accounted for as a change in interest transaction.
Upon Settlement, the company sold approximately 9.7&nbsp;million of its ordinary shares in JDE Peet&#146;s in the offering for gross proceeds of &#128;304&nbsp;million ($343 million). The company subsequently sold approximately 1.4&nbsp;million
additional shares and received gross proceeds of &#128;46&nbsp;million ($51 million) upon exercise of the over-allotment option. Following Settlement and the exercise of the over-allotment option, the company held a 22.9% equity interest in JDE
Peet&#146;s. During the second quarter of 2020, the company recorded a preliminary gain of $121&nbsp;million, net of $33&nbsp;million released from accumulated other comprehensive losses, and incurred $48&nbsp;million of transaction costs. The
company also incurred a $261&nbsp;million tax expense that is payable in 2020 and 2021. During the third quarter of 2020, the company increased its preliminary gain by $10&nbsp;million to $131&nbsp;million. During the fourth quarter of 2020, the
company recorded a $7&nbsp;million loss related to a minor dilution of its ownership percentage and reduced its tax expense by $11&nbsp;million to $250&nbsp;million. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">In connection with this transaction, during the second quarter of 2020, the company changed its accounting principle to reflect its share of JDE&#146;s
historical and JDE Peet&#146;s ongoing earnings on a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">one-quarter</FONT> lag basis, although the company continues to record dividends when cash is received. The company determined a lag was preferable as it enables
the company to continue to report its quarterly and annual results on a timely basis, while recording its share of JDE Peet&#146;s ongoing results after JDE Peet&#146;s has publicly reported its results. This change in accounting principle was
applied retrospectively to all periods. In addition, the company considers the 3.6% ownership reduction a partial divestiture of its equity method investment in JDE Peet&#146;s. Therefore, the company has removed the equity method investment net
earnings related to this divested portion from its <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial results for Adjusted EPS for all historical periods presented to facilitate comparison of results. The company&#146;s U.S. GAAP results,
which include its equity method investment net earnings from JDE Peet&#146;s, did not change from what was previously reported. </P>
</DIV></Center>


<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always">
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">


<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Equity method investee items </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Within Adjusted EPS, the company&#146;s equity method investment net earnings exclude its proportionate share of its equity method investees&#146; significant
operating and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-operating</FONT> items, such as acquisition and divestiture-related costs and restructuring program costs. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Constant currency </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Management evaluates the
operating performance of the company and its international subsidiaries on a constant currency basis. The company determines its constant currency operating results by dividing or multiplying, as appropriate, the current period local currency
operating results by the currency exchange rates used to translate the company&#146;s financial statements in the comparable prior-year period to determine what the current-period U.S. dollar operating results would have been if the currency
exchange rate had not changed from the comparable prior-year period. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>OUTLOOK </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company&#146;s outlook for 2021 Organic Net Revenue growth, Adjusted EPS growth on a constant currency basis and Free Cash Flow are <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures that exclude or otherwise adjust for items impacting comparability of financial results such as the impact of changes in currency exchange rates, restructuring activities, acquisitions
and divestitures. The company is not able to reconcile its projected Organic Net Revenue growth to its projected reported net revenue growth for the full-year 2021 because the company is unable to predict during this period the impact from potential
acquisitions or divestitures, as well as the impact of currency translation due to the unpredictability of future changes in currency exchange rates, which could be material as a significant portion of the company&#146;s operations are outside the
U.S. The company is not able to reconcile its projected Adjusted EPS growth on a constant currency basis to its projected reported diluted EPS growth for the full-year 2021 because the company is unable to predict during this period the timing of
its restructuring program costs, <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> impacts from commodity and forecasted currency transaction derivative contracts and impacts from potential acquisitions
or divestitures as well as the impact of currency translation due to the unpredictability of future changes in currency exchange rates, which could be material as a significant portion of the company&#146;s operations are outside the U.S. The
company is not able to reconcile its projected Free Cash Flow to its projected net cash from operating activities for the full-year 2021 because the company is unable to predict during this period the timing and amount of capital expenditures
impacting cash flow. Therefore, because of the uncertainty and variability of the nature and amount of future adjustments, which could be significant, the company is unable to provide a reconciliation of these measures without unreasonable effort.
</P>
</DIV></Center>
